  //<![CDATA[
    function loadScript(url, callback) {
      var script = document.createElement("script");
      script.type = "text/javascript";
    
      if (script.readyState) {  //Internet Explorer
          script.onreadystatechange = function() {
            if (script.readyState == "loaded" ||
                    script.readyState == "complete") {
              script.onreadystatechange = null;
              callback();
            }
          };
      } else {  //Other browsers
        script.onload = function() {
          callback();
        };
      }
    
      script.src = url;
      document.getElementsByTagName("head")[0].appendChild(script);
    }
    
    function initAppleId() {
      AppleID.auth.init({
        clientId : 'com.goodreads.app', 
        scope : 'name email',
        redirectURI: 'https://www.goodreads.com/apple_users/sign_in_with_apple_web',
        state: 'apple_oauth_state_27679ec5-435f-4159-ae86-b71a4e628b08'
      });
    }
    
    var initializeSiwa = function() {
      var APPLE_SIGN_IN_JS_URL =  "https://appleid.cdn-apple.com/appleauth/static/jsapi/appleid/1/en_US/appleid.auth.js"
      loadScript(APPLE_SIGN_IN_JS_URL, initAppleId);
    };

<span id="freeTextContainer6571439577317686780"><i>Librarian's note: An alternate cover edition can be found <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/54787609.here' title='here' rel='nofollow noopener'>here</a></i><br/><br/>At school Connell and Marianne pretend not to know each other. But when Connell comes to pick his mother up from her housekeeping job at Marianne’s house, a strange and indelible connection grows bet</span>
  <span id="freeText6571439577317686780" style="display:none"><i>Librarian's note: An alternate cover edition can be found <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/54787609.here" title="here" rel="nofollow noopener">here</a></i><br /><br />At school Connell and Marianne pretend not to know each other. He’s popular and well-adjusted, star of the school soccer team while she is lonely, proud, and intensely private. But when Connell comes to pick his mother up from her housekeeping job at Marianne’s house, a strange and indelible connection grows between the two teenagers - one they are determined to conceal.<br /><br />A year later, they’re both studying at Trinity College in Dublin. Marianne has found her feet in a new social world while Connell hangs at the sidelines, shy and uncertain. Throughout their years in college, Marianne and Connell circle one another, straying toward other people and possibilities but always magnetically, irresistibly drawn back together. Then, as she veers into self-destruction and he begins to search for meaning elsewhere, each must confront how far they are willing to go to save the other.<br /><br />Sally Rooney brings her brilliant psychological acuity and perfectly spare prose to a story that explores the subtleties of class, the electricity of first love, and the complex entanglements of family and friendship.</span>
  <a data-text-id="6571439577317686780" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

<div class='communityQuestion'>
<div class='questionText'>
<div class='spoiler'>
This question contains spoilers…
<span class='spoilerAnswerText'>
<a href="/questions/1512955-so-i-am-just-getting-to-the-point-in-this"><a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[So I am just getting to the point in this where Marianne has started to eat less and less, fixating on her food and savouring it. Essentially, it reads like she's moving towards anorexia if she hasn't already. Without giving too much away, does it have a happier ending? Does she get therapy? I know too many people with severe mental health problems in real life to want to read further if it doesn't :( <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span></a>
</span>
</div>

<div class='allCommunityAnswers'>
<div class='communityAnswer'>
<div class='communityAnswerBody'>
<div class='answererUserIcon'>
<a class="leftAlignedImage userPhoto" href="/user/show/77074345-towhid-islam"><img alt="" src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/users/1517187998i/77074345._UX100_CR0,0,100,100_.jpg" /></a>
</div>
<div class='communityAnswerTextContainer'>
<span class='communityAnswererName'>
<a href="/user/show/77074345-towhid-islam">Towhid Islam</a>
</span>
<span class='communityAnswerText'>
<span class="expandableContainer"><span class="truncatedContent">That's one opinion/interpretation of the ending (of the novel). I for one, couldn't ask for a better ending, because the author let each one of us, re<a class="jsShow showAction" href="#">…more</a></span><span class="fullContent">That's one opinion/interpretation of the ending (of the novel). I for one, couldn't ask for a better ending, because the author let each one of us, readers, to imagine however we wish to believe how the story of Connell and Marianne shall continue. While such an ending presents an opportunity for a sequel for the author (after all, she needs to eat), I couldn't have asked for more. To continue on and read about these two people go their separate ways once more and get back together again, would be dull and boring.<br /><br />My interpretation of the ending, is that both have matured sufficiently to recognize and accept these two people are at their best when they are together. Therefore, in my imagination, Connell would simply refuse to go to NYU without Marianne. Perhaps he would convince her to apply for a master's program at NYU as well and would only embark on his MFA, if Marianne was accepted so that they would be together. Or, if Marianne had no further interest in (higher) education, Connell would find a master's program nearby so that they could continue to be together. I remember, it is only Connell who keeps on telling Marianne that he loves her, whereas she barely says so, just once. In the last few pages the author revealed that Marianne finally realized that she is truly herself only when she is with Connell. I expect these two to grow old together.<a class="jsHide hideAction" href="#">(less)</a></span></span>
</span>
</div>
</div>

<div id="review_2679601484" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2679601484" />
    <a title="Emily May" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/4622890-emily-may"><img alt="Emily May" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1528390751p2/4622890.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2679601484?book_show_action=true">Jan 18, 2019</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Emily May" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Emily May" href="/user/show/4622890-emily-may">Emily May</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Hardcover 9780571334643" href="/book/show/37539457-normal-people">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4622890-emily-may?shelf=2019">2019</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4622890-emily-may?shelf=contemporary">contemporary</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2679601484" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer8452970750520901408"><blockquote>
  <i>No one can be independent of other people completely, so why not give up the attempt, she thought, go running in the other direction, depend on people for everything, allow them to depend on you, why not.</i>
</blockquote><br/>This is going to be a polarizing book. I mean, I <i>think</i> I liked it. And I say "liked it" in the sense that it made me very miserable. It is a quiet character study, almost a YA novel but not quite, and it is a <b>profoundly lonely and depressing love story</b>.<br/><br/>I didn't begin by liking it. <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/37539457.Normal_People' title='Normal People by Sally Rooney' rel='nofollow noopener'>Normal Peo</a></span>
  <span id="freeText8452970750520901408" style="display:none"><blockquote>
  <i>No one can be independent of other people completely, so why not give up the attempt, she thought, go running in the other direction, depend on people for everything, allow them to depend on you, why not.</i>
</blockquote><br />This is going to be a polarizing book. I mean, I <i>think</i> I liked it. And I say "liked it" in the sense that it made me very miserable. It is a quiet character study, almost a YA novel but not quite, and it is a <b>profoundly lonely and depressing love story</b>.<br /><br />I didn't begin by liking it. <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/37539457.Normal_People" title="Normal People by Sally Rooney" rel="nofollow noopener">Normal People</a> follows two characters - Marianne and Connell - through adolescence and into early adulthood, and they begin by being the kind of uber-precocious teenagers who read Proust and Marx for fun. It took a while for me to settle into their story. My initial impression was that this was going to be some kind of <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/1406384.John_Green" title="John Green" rel="nofollow noopener">John Green</a> for adults, which is not something that floats my particular boat.<br /><br />Without fully realizing it though, this book had crept quietly under my skin. The relationship between Marianne and Connell is angsty, sure, but it felt painfully real. They are so flawed, marred by unlikable characteristics, and yet, <b>I could not stop caring about them</b>.<br /><blockquote>
  <i>Not for the first time Marianne thinks cruelty does not only hurt the victim, but the perpetrator also, and maybe more deeply and more permanently. You learn nothing very profound about yourself simply by being bullied; but by bullying someone else you learn something you can never forget.</i>
</blockquote><br />The story is really just about the two of them and their relationship. In high school, Marianne is a smart and wealthy girl, but is socially ostracized and emotionally abused at home, whereas Connell is working class, but very popular. Connell's mum works as a cleaner for Marianne's family. They begin a secret sexual relationship that falls apart when Connell fears his friends will find out. The compelling dynamic between them drives the story-- issues of class and social status cause much conflict.<br /><br />In college, the two meet again. This time, Marianne is popular, and Connell is feeling increasingly depressed. The two of them lean on each other time and again as they move through a social world filled with social expectations. There's a bit of a <i>When Harry Met Sally</i> vibe, except that this book is more soul-destroying.<br /><blockquote>
  <i>Nothing had meant more to Rob than the approval of others; to be thought well of, to be a person of status. He would have betrayed any confidence, any kindness, for the promise of social acceptance.</i>
</blockquote><br />There's clear criticism of our constant need to impress and perform for others in a world that grows ever more connected. Much of the tragedy that befalls Marianne and Connell is caused by other people, peer pressure and social expectations. It is very sad to think that someone might give up who they love the most because they can't deal with how it makes them look to others.<br /><br />The pair's inability to adequately communicate is frustrating but feels realistic. I was on the verge of tearing my hair out at all the things left unsaid in this book, but I think it was a good kind of frustration. The kind that comes from caring too much. <br /><br />I feel like there are any number of reasons I could have hated <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/37539457.Normal_People" title="Normal People by Sally Rooney" rel="nofollow noopener">Normal People</a>, but I didn’t. I actually kinda loved it. It's a weird, awkward, depressing novel about a connection formed between two very different people who find exactly what they need - and perhaps a lot that they don't - in each other. <br /><br />CW: sexual assault; domestic abuse; drug use; casual racism (called out); depression; anxiety; suicide &amp; suicidal ideation.<br /><br /><a href="http://emilymay.me" rel="nofollow noopener">Blog</a> | <a href="https://www.facebook.com/thebookgeekreviews" rel="nofollow noopener">Facebook</a> | <a href="https://twitter.com/thebookgeek01" rel="nofollow noopener">Twitter</a> | <a href="http://instagram.com/emleemay" rel="nofollow noopener">Instagram</a> | <a href="https://www.youtube.com/c/EmilyMayTheBookGeek" rel="nofollow noopener">Youtube</a></span>
  <a data-text-id="8452970750520901408" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

    <div class="section">
      

<div id="review_2445724332" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2445724332" />
    <a title="Marchpane" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/6677659-marchpane"><img alt="Marchpane" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1483537315p2/6677659.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2445724332?book_show_action=true">Sep 07, 2018</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Marchpane" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Marchpane" href="/user/show/6677659-marchpane">Marchpane</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Kindle Edition " href="/book/show/40648401-normal-people">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/6677659-marchpane?shelf=19-20-19">19-20-19</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/6677659-marchpane?shelf=book-club">book-club</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2445724332" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer9948105440896605048"><b>Sally Rooney is the real deal</b><br/><br/><i>Normal People</i> has been lavished with praise from critics, longlisted for the Man Booker prize and <a href='https://www.irishtimes.com/culture/film/lenny-abrahamson-to-direct-sally-rooney-adaptation-for-bbc-1.3604072' rel='nofollow noopener'>adapted for television by the BBC</a>. And that's just in its first week of publication! <br/><br/>All that attention will, no doubt, attract quite a few readers who would not ordinarily touch this subject with a barge pole. Because this book:<br/><br/>A)	Is about young people<br/>B)	Is a love story (but not a 'romance novel')<br/>C)	Contains a fair bit of sex (which is crucial to the storytelling, btw, </span>
  <span id="freeText9948105440896605048" style="display:none"><b>Sally Rooney is the real deal</b><br /><br /><i>Normal People</i> has been lavished with praise from critics, longlisted for the Man Booker prize and <a href="https://www.irishtimes.com/culture/film/lenny-abrahamson-to-direct-sally-rooney-adaptation-for-bbc-1.3604072" rel="nofollow noopener">adapted for television by the BBC</a>. And that's just in its first week of publication! <br /><br />All that attention will, no doubt, attract quite a few readers who would not ordinarily touch this subject with a barge pole. Because this book:<br /><br />A)	Is about young people<br />B)	Is a love story (but not a 'romance novel')<br />C)	Contains a fair bit of sex (which is crucial to the storytelling, btw, and is not graphic)<br /><br />All of which (possibly also the fact that the author is a 27-year-old woman) means that <i>Normal People</i> will inevitably be dismissed by some as frivolous. It isn’t. This is a confident, accomplished and serious work. <br /><br />Of Rooney’s debut, <i>Conversations with Friends</i>, I said in my review it ‘occasionally scrapes close to the bone’. Well, <i>Normal People</i> cuts to the core.<br /><br /><i>Normal People</i> is not out to inspire, instruct, entertain or talk down to anyone, which makes it something of a refreshing anomaly in current fiction about young people. It is a novel (for anyone, young or old) that simply presents the truth of youthful experiences without the filters of nostalgia or sentimentality. It invites you to inhabit the psyche of someone else – two someone elses: Connell and Marianne – to identify with them and to feel their pain and turmoil. For the reader who connects to that, it is wracking. <br /><br />The story focuses only on the pivotal moments for these two characters, jumping forward three weeks, six months, or five minutes, as needed, to excise all the uneventful bits of life and leave us with the most emotionally intense supercut possible. It follows them from high school in a small town, through their years at university in Dublin, as the dynamic between them shifts with their surroundings and social circle. They’re not officially 'together' the whole time, or even most of the time, but they always figure in each other’s lives in a significant way.<br /><br />Sally Rooney writes with such precision that this all feels painfully true. She conjures the tension and emotion in a scene just from the way someone wrings out a dish sponge; she conveys the full weight of feeling from a look or a shrug. In Rooney’s imagining, Connell and Marianne as separate entities are less important than the interplay between them – their relationship dynamic and the influence each of them has on shaping the other, that’s the real stuff of this book: <br /><br /><blockquote>
  <i>"How strange to feel herself so completely under the control of another person, but also how ordinary. No one can be independent of other people completely, so why not give up the attempt, she thought, go running in the other direction, depend on people for everything, allow them to depend on you, why not."</i>
  <br />
</blockquote><br /><br />There’s irony here, and self-conscious posturing (though not nearly as much as in CWF), but earnestness, truth and kindness as well. In addition to the central relationship are issues of class and intellectual integrity. It's a particularly astute look at the rebuild of self that teenagers undergo in the transition from school to uni, how it allows some to thrive while others stumble, and in some ways is just an illusion after all. <br /><br />So there’s hype and there’s backlash to the hype, and <i>Normal People</i> is sure to resonate powerfully with some readers and not at all for others. If you like a minutely observed novel about people and feelings that isn’t mawkish, I'd say give it a go.</span>
  <a data-text-id="9948105440896605048" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

    <div class="section">
      

<div id="review_2519494611" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2519494611" />
    <a title="Bernard O&#39;Keeffe" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/15171195-bernard-o-keeffe"><img alt="Bernard O&#39;Keeffe" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1442879919p2/15171195.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2519494611?book_show_action=true">Sep 04, 2018</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Bernard O&#39;Keeffe" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Bernard O&#39;Keeffe" href="/user/show/15171195-bernard-o-keeffe">Bernard O&#39;Keeffe</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="did not like it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">did not like it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Hardcover 9780571334643" href="/book/show/37539457-normal-people">review of another edition</a>


        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2519494611" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer3053552346908283576">On the second page of Sally Rooney’s universally acclaimed, Booker- longlisted novel is the following paragraph:<br/><br/>‘He puts his hands in his pockets and suppresses an irritable sigh, but suppresses it with an audible intake of breath, so that it still sounds like a sigh.’<br/><br/>What?<br/><br/>I get the hand in the pockets bit, but how the hell does the rest of it work? A sigh is an exhalation and I have no idea how any attempt to suppress a sigh by inhaling could possibly sound like one. I’ve tried hard to imagine </span>
  <span id="freeText3053552346908283576" style="display:none">On the second page of Sally Rooney’s universally acclaimed, Booker- longlisted novel is the following paragraph:<br /><br />‘He puts his hands in his pockets and suppresses an irritable sigh, but suppresses it with an audible intake of breath, so that it still sounds like a sigh.’<br /><br />What?<br /><br />I get the hand in the pockets bit, but how the hell does the rest of it work? A sigh is an exhalation and I have no idea how any attempt to suppress a sigh by inhaling could possibly sound like one. I’ve tried hard to imagine it, but no luck. I’ve tried even harder to do it, but even less luck. In fact, in an effort to understand this twaddle I have tried it so often that I have come close on several occasions to hyperventilating and passing out.<br /><br />What have those Faber editors been doing? Maybe they have no problem with it because they are all so much cleverer than me and know how to read properly. Or maybe they also tried to do it and actually did pass out, which might explain why they have failed to apply the editorial pencil with any intelligence in the 264 pages that follow.<br /><br />The more likely explanation, of course, is that the problem is mine – and I offer the following gems from Normal People on that understanding… <br /><br />• ‘He looks down into his lap, and exhales quickly, almost like a cough’.<br /><br />It’s hyperventilation time again. I’ve imagined it and I’ve tried it, but I still don’t get it. <br /><br />• ‘He can’t even visually imagine himself as a lawyer, wearing a tie and so on..’<br /><br />Do we really need that ‘visually’? <br /><br />• ‘It’s true she is Connell’s type, maybe even the originary model of the type:’<br /><br />Originary? What does that mean? Am I the only one who had to look it up? (It’s not in Chambers, by the way, so you’ll need the OED) <br /><br />• ‘Peggy, watching, took a performatively large mouthful of Cointreau…’<br /><br />Can anyone explain what ‘performatively large’ actually means?<br /><br />• ‘Enraged now, Alan wrenched her back from the sink by her upper arm, and, seemingly spontaneously, spat at her.’<br /><br />Seemingly spontaneously? <br /><br />I could go on. It’s not often that I feel the need to read with a pencil in my hand but Normal People drove me to it, and my copy is now covered with question marks and annotations. I retired from teaching last year but reading Sally Rooney’s feted novel felt like I was marking again - in this case marking the work of a precocious, but overindulged, talent.<br /><br />In 'Normal People' alternating points of view are combined with an inconsistent and confusing authorial presence, voices are often difficult to differentiate in an ineffectual free indirect style, the comma splices (Ferrante this isn’t) and the unpunctuated dialogue, far from creating an impressionistic flow, suggest a lack of precision, and the prose shifts from past to present for no apparent reason and even within paragraphs, creating a chronological blur. In short, it's a bit of a mess. <br /><br />If I cared about the characters or cared about the story, these things would not matter quite so much but on the few occasions when I saw through the writerly mess I found it difficult to care about them at all.<br /><br />The novel, though, has been so well received that its very reception has become a news story. ‘Salinger for the Snapchat generation’: critics unite to praise 27 year-old novelist’ was the headline in last Saturday’s Guardian.<br /><br />So the problem is clearly mine. <br />Maybe I've read a different book from the one everyone is raving about. Maybe I've read the same book but don't know how to read properly. Or it could be that I'm the child's voice at the back of the crowd politely suggesting that the emperor might not be wearing any clothes.</span>
  <a data-text-id="3053552346908283576" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_2507265266" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2507265266" />
    <a title="Trudie" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/4617856-trudie"><img alt="Trudie" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1586207854p2/4617856.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2507265266?book_show_action=true">Sep 24, 2018</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Trudie" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Trudie" href="/user/show/4617856-trudie">Trudie</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="did not like it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">did not like it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9780571347292" href="/book/show/40178403-normal-people">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4617856-trudie?shelf=booker-18">booker-18</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2507265266" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer9843605334572741652">I am not sure how to write this review because I seem to be so far beyond the pale on my antipathy to this book. In simplest terms I didn't connect with this work at all and I would be best to chalk this up to a "reader/writer" mismatch and move on but I will try and articulate some of my reading experience.<br/><br/>Some of my perplexity with <i>Normal People</i> is that I just couldn't relate to the twenty something, highly educated, politically aware and cynical young adults that populate this novel. I am not</span>
  <span id="freeText9843605334572741652" style="display:none">I am not sure how to write this review because I seem to be so far beyond the pale on my antipathy to this book. In simplest terms I didn't connect with this work at all and I would be best to chalk this up to a "reader/writer" mismatch and move on but I will try and articulate some of my reading experience.<br /><br />Some of my perplexity with <i>Normal People</i> is that I just couldn't relate to the twenty something, highly educated, politically aware and cynical young adults that populate this novel. I am not sure how reflective these voices are of young Irish making their way in the world, but as presented here I found them exasperating to listen to and not particularly nuanced. <br />It is possible that even if I didn't enjoy the novel I might like the writing but in actual fact Rooney's style is perhaps the single biggest thing that bugged me. I found some passages of interest sandwiched between a lot of wooden dialogue and these flat descriptions ...<br /><br /><i> Marianne goes inside and comes back out again with another bottle of sparkling wine, and one bottle of red. Niall starts unwrapping the wire on the first bottle and Marianne hands Connell a corkscrew. Peggy starts clearing people's plates. Connell unpeels the foil from the top of a bottle as Jamie leans over and says something to Marianne. He sinks the screw into the cork and twists it downwards. Peggy takes his plate away and stacks it with the others </i><br /><br />This kind of writing really gives me nothing. <br /><br />Others have cited the two dimensional nature of her secondary characters and I would concur. Barely any of them made much of an impression on me. Alan - Marianne's brother, seemed particularly badly drawn. He appears to be a key part of understanding Marianne and yet he warrants only a few pen-strokes of unexplained malice and cruelty. The opening of a wine-bottle and pouring of cups of tea receives much more page space. <br /><br />I tried to understand Marianne, who seems to be both ugly and beautiful, popular and friendless. Her hinted at troubled family life was suppose to underpin her need to be a submissive. I remain unconvinced that this is really how dominance and submission works and I would think experts in BDSM might strongly take issue with some of the cliches here. <br /><br />The relationship between Marianne and Connell should have kept this book afloat at the very least. The intense emotional and physical connection, the will they / won't they stay together, all the drama of YA love is here but it is in an eye-wateringly navel-gazing form. I found it all exactingly po-faced. The number of inexplicable break-ups, largely based on mis-communication was about three or four break-ups too many for me. I just wanted to yell at this novel most of the time. Say what you mean and stop being so insufferably difficult !, either split up or stay together, both your friends and I really don't care !. Marianne and Connell were of most interest to me when they started emailing each other, discussing novels and politics thus preventing them breaking up over some new emotional minutiae. Perhaps this should have been a novel of their email exchanges.<br /><br />Oh well, I guess I will never be a Rooney fan and I have doubtless missed the point of this book entirely but that is ok not every book is for every reader.</span>
  <a data-text-id="9843605334572741652" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2829764002?book_show_action=true">May 30, 2019</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Justin" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Justin" href="/user/show/2795921-justin">Justin</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="did not like it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">did not like it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Hardcover 9780571334643" href="/book/show/37539457-normal-people">review of another edition</a>


        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2829764002" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer14083160968388534042">Whoa... guys... I just finished Normal... man, I just... I don’t know... what am I, what am I, uh, missing? This, uh, this... this wasn’t good. Not good at all. I’m so confused. This is, um, this is... this book is everywhere right now, being highly praised and all that. Websites I trust are telling me this is, this is one of the best, one of the best books of the year so far. But, guys... wow. <br/><br/>I’ve never felt more disconnected from a story. I couldn’t care less about either one of these charact</span>
  <span id="freeText14083160968388534042" style="display:none">Whoa... guys... I just finished Normal... man, I just... I don’t know... what am I, what am I, uh, missing? This, uh, this... this wasn’t good. Not good at all. I’m so confused. This is, um, this is... this book is everywhere right now, being highly praised and all that. Websites I trust are telling me this is, this is one of the best, one of the best books of the year so far. But, guys... wow. <br /><br />I’ve never felt more disconnected from a story. I couldn’t care less about either one of these characters, and I definitely didn’t care about anyone else in the book because, man, I don’t think the author cared either. This whole thing just felt lifeless to me, like it wanted to be something huge (and it sure is being pushed like it is), but there is really nothing about this book I found redeeming. I hung around until the end thinking something would resolve or the story would progress somehow, but it just kind of fizzles out and it’s done. I wish it would have at least ended with an apology for taking up too much space in the crowded book world. <br /><br />Seriously, the whole back and forth of I love you, let’s have sex, do whatever you want, we’re different, I can’t tell anyone about you, I love you, I’m seeing someone else, I’m so sad, life is hard, being 20 is tough... that is basically the book. It just kind of bounces around those themes over and over again. There’s nothing in the book to make me care if these kids are in love or not, and it really feels like this should be a YA novel, but it pushed the characters ages up just a bit to say “Nope, no no no... adults here. We have adults coming through! This is Adult Fiction folks! It reads like Twilight without the vampires, but someone give this bad boy a Man Booker prize! Adult book here, ladies and gentlemen! Don’t get it twisted!” <br /><br />I don’t get it. I didn’t connect with this at all, and I would recommend steering clear of this one and moving on to something else on your list. As my old librarian used to say... “So little books, so little time”. He’s the only person who has ever said that. I think he trademarked it. He’s right. Skip this.</span>
  <a data-text-id="14083160968388534042" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">

              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer2361971983562411753"><b> Man booker prize long list nominee and Costa book awards nominee This is a book that has many admirers and sadly it didn't work for me and while I would love to agree with all the judges on this one I only struggled to the end because it was a bookclub read. It is difficult to go against the grain on a book that is nominated for so many awards. So as always <u>you </u> need to judge for yourself because books fit people differently </b> <br/><br/>Quite simply this book didn't <u> Fit Me</u>. I really have no interest in r</span>
  <span id="freeText2361971983562411753" style="display:none"><b> Man booker prize long list nominee and Costa book awards nominee This is a book that has many admirers and sadly it didn't work for me and while I would love to agree with all the judges on this one I only struggled to the end because it was a bookclub read. It is difficult to go against the grain on a book that is nominated for so many awards. So as always <u>you </u> need to judge for yourself because books fit people differently </b> <br /><br />Quite simply this book didn't <u> Fit Me</u>. I really have no interest in reading about 18-20 something year college kid's on/off sexual relationships where they seem to only exist in their own little complex bubble and this book felt like a bubble. It is described as "exquisite love stroy" which I honestly found nothing exquisite or no love in this one. <br /><br />The characters of Connell and Marianne were dislikable and boring and the on / off, will they wont they "relationship" became repetitive reading. The only character which I liked and felt any connection with in the novel was Lorraine.<br /><br />Perhaps this is more suited for a younger audience where they connect with the college scene or for readers who like complex relationship stories but for me this was a struggle from start to finish.</span>

<div id="review_2517248338" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2517248338" />
    <a title="Anna Luce" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/9429655-anna-luce"><img alt="Anna Luce" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1604227738p2/9429655.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2517248338?book_show_action=true">Sep 04, 2018</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Anna Luce" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Anna Luce" href="/user/show/9429655-anna-luce">Anna Luce</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Audiobook " href="/book/show/41642870-normal-people">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/9429655-anna-luce?shelf=audiobooks">audiobooks</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/9429655-anna-luce?shelf=2018-reviews">2018-reviews</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/9429655-anna-luce?shelf=disappointing-reads">disappointing-reads</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/9429655-anna-luce?shelf=inane-protagonists">inane-protagonists</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/9429655-anna-luce?shelf=6-so-so-reads">6-so-so-reads</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2517248338" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer16164406845702384527">★★✰✰✰ 2 grungy stars<br/><br/><b>If you believe that characters who dislike themselves, shrug a lot, and say "I don't know" 24/7, are very deep and realistic, well this may be the perfect read for you.</b> <br/>Or if you enjoy reading about "in" authors...look no further. After all, Rooney is "defining a generation".<br/><br/>If you are thinking about reading this novel, I suggest you listen to the following song instead, since it will take you less time and you will get the same story:<br/><a target='_blank' rel='noopener nofollow' href='https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=BjMwdL5WtFc'>https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=BjMwd...</a><br/><br/><b>W</b></span>
  <span id="freeText16164406845702384527" style="display:none">★★✰✰✰ 2 grungy stars<br /><br /><b>If you believe that characters who dislike themselves, shrug a lot, and say "I don't know" 24/7, are very deep and realistic, well this may be the perfect read for you.</b> <br />Or if you enjoy reading about "in" authors...look no further. After all, Rooney is "defining a generation".<br /><br />If you are thinking about reading this novel, I suggest you listen to the following song instead, since it will take you less time and you will get the same story:<br /><a target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow" href="https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=BjMwdL5WtFc">https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=BjMwd...</a><br /><br /><b>While I enjoyed Rooney's style, the way in which she interweaves ordinary moments with emotionally charged ones and the uncertainty that pervades her story, I was also annoyed by how artificial her novel is</b>. I had the impression that <b>Rooney was trying to conjure a certain millennial "vibe" through her characters and their experiences. </b><br />However, the central figures of her novel, Connell and Marianne, lacked depth and, as stupid as it might sound, character. <b>Their looks were emphasised in a way that made them "stand out" from others: they are skinny and beautiful, they smoke, they make languid movements, they are smart, and unlike their peers they actually care about world politics. Throughout the course of this novel we are told how DIFFERENT and SPECIAL they are</b>. <br />Marianne comes from a wealthy and abusive family (we are supposed to feel bad for her), Connell was raised by his mother and suffers from bouts of anxiety and depression (we are also supposed to feel bad for him).<b> That they have issues that they can't cope with is realistic, but what I didn't appreciate is<u> the romanticising of their difficulties</u>. What I didn't like is that being "alienated" is synonym of "cool" and that seeking sadomasochistic relationships is understandable/inevitable if you come from an abusive family</b>. <br />Rooney handles serious issues (eg. an abusive family, depression, etc.) very badly. <b>A book that handles trauma and self-harming incredibly well is <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/41087365.What_Red_Was" title="What Red Was by Rosie Price" rel="nofollow noopener">What Red Was</a> by <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/18284700.Rosie_Price" title="Rosie Price" rel="nofollow noopener">Rosie Price</a>. </b>There we see <b>why </b>the characters behave in self-destructive ways, but in NP these things seem <b>merely props</b>.<br />Marianne and Connell aren't terrible people but god, they are so self-involved. Their relationship is made to appear fraught but I didn't always understand why. <b>Drama for the sake of drama?</b> They enter forgettable relationships with equally forgettable people but they remain fixated on each other.<i> Why? </i>No one knows...<br />Marianne is depicted by the author and the other characters as being the sort of person who does not to care about others' opinion of her but soon after a breakup with a cliched dick boyfriend she is obsessed with what people are saying about her...Connor is...intelligent? Indecisive? As interesting as a stale sandwich?!<br /><b>Secondary characters and family members are barely sketched out</b>, they have little to no purpose other than creating more "drama" for the main characters. Marianne's family was so badly written that I had a hard time taking any of them seriously. Her brother is laughably cruel and her mother is uncaring and snobbish (they are rich so...). Friends from college serve very little purpose, other than making the main characters seem "different" and "real" (they are special, not like other people).<br /><b>What I disliked the most is that by the end neither Marianne or Connell show any sort of character growth. </b> Not that I always want to read about characters who learn from their mistakes or gain some sort of insight from their experience,<b> I can appreciate characters who keep perpetuating their 'bad' behaviour or even those who get worse or regress into 'bad' habits/behaviour. But <u>they have to be believable</u>. Marianne or Connell were not. </b>They were merely an 'aesthetic', <b>more befitting as subjects of a black and white grunge photo than anything else. </b><br />The only reason why I finished this novel is that <b>I listened to the audiobook and the narrator managed to make this otherwise unappetising storyline sort of okay.</b></span>
  <a data-text-id="16164406845702384527" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2800293973" />
    <a title="jessica" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/10171516-jessica"><img alt="jessica" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1509983330p2/10171516.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2800293973?book_show_action=true">Apr 29, 2019</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="jessica" class="user" itemprop="url" name="jessica" href="/user/show/10171516-jessica">jessica</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9780571334650" href="/book/show/41086877-normal-people">review of another edition</a>


        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2800293973" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer4320186249917012400">wow. one of the most frustrating, but humanising, books i have read in a long time. for sure. i feel so exhausted after reading this, but i think that may have been the authors intent. its shows that normal people living normal lives can be quite tiresome. for example:<br/><br/>- the writing lacks quotation marks, which makes the dialogue difficult to decipher. which could be seen as support for the idea that life is just as messy as the books formatting and communication sometimes takes effort to underst</span>
  <span id="freeText4320186249917012400" style="display:none">wow. one of the most frustrating, but humanising, books i have read in a long time. for sure. i feel so exhausted after reading this, but i think that may have been the authors intent. its shows that normal people living normal lives can be quite tiresome. for example:<br /><br />- the writing lacks quotation marks, which makes the dialogue difficult to decipher. which could be seen as support for the idea that life is just as messy as the books formatting and communication sometimes takes effort to understand. <br /><br />- there are massive jumps in the timeline with a lot of backtracking, so much so that the drastic shifts are jarring. which could be seen as exemplifying the notion that people change over time and friendships are bound to alter.<br /><br />things like this will polarise readers. either its too much and unenjoyable, or its a work of genius and adds depth to the storytelling. i think it really depends on the readers interpretation and mood. and like the indecisive creature that i am, im quite torn down the middle. <br /><br /><b>↠ <i>3.5 stars</i></b></span>
  <a data-text-id="4320186249917012400" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  <span id="freeText12742522920794738428" style="display:none">You were slightly harsher than me (I gave it 2 stars) but I completely agree. I know there has been some pushback recently that unlikeable characters don't make a book bad, but I just can't deal with reading about main characters I hate. I read this books about a year ago, but from memory Connell wasn't too awful, and I cared about his storyline much more than Marianne's. She was just annoying and confusing. I hated the will they/won't they things that took up, to be honest, basically the whole book. Just overall, I don't get it. It's very rare that I rate a book under a 3 star, and ever rarer that I genuinely don't see how anyone enjoyed it but... this book fits both.</span>

<div id="review_2742921511" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2742921511" />
    <a title="Cindy" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/57797254-cindy"><img alt="Cindy" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1598112512p2/57797254.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2742921511?book_show_action=true">Jul 24, 2020</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Cindy" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Cindy" href="/user/show/57797254-cindy">Cindy</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2742921511" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer15936298840230707784">The book aims to hit emotional poignancy by showing how people weave in and out of your life and exploring themes of first love, class differences, and depression; but ultimately the narrative boils down to two co-dependent people hooking up throughout the years, which doesn't really add anything new. Turn to your social circle IRL and you'll find the same story.</span>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_2520750544" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2520750544" />
    <a title="Elyse  Walters" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/597461-elyse-walters"><img alt="Elyse  Walters" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1514246949p2/597461.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2520750544?book_show_action=true">May 21, 2019</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Elyse  Walters" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Elyse  Walters" href="/user/show/597461-elyse-walters">Elyse  Walters</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Hardcover 9780571334643" href="/book/show/37539457-normal-people">review of another edition</a>


        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2520750544" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer561271467641569558">I had been influenced by a friend - whom I adore & respect - by her 1 star review.... way before this book started gaining momentum and hit the stores a month ago. <br/>This book wasn’t for my friend - but it sure was for me. <br/><br/>I’ve own an ‘Advance Reader’s Edition’, of Sally Rooney’s paper copy for a year and a half. It sat on my shelf, unread. <br/><br/>Rooney’s first novel “Conversations With Friends”, was wonderful. <br/><br/>I admit having a thing for the type of writer Sally Rooney is:<br/>*Addicting* thought-provoking r</span>
  <span id="freeText561271467641569558" style="display:none">I had been influenced by a friend - whom I adore &amp; respect - by her 1 star review.... way before this book started gaining momentum and hit the stores a month ago. <br />This book wasn’t for my friend - but it sure was for me. <br /><br />I’ve own an ‘Advance Reader’s Edition’, of Sally Rooney’s paper copy for a year and a half. It sat on my shelf, unread. <br /><br />Rooney’s first novel “Conversations With Friends”, was wonderful. <br /><br />I admit having a thing for the type of writer Sally Rooney is:<br />*Addicting* thought-provoking reading for me. “Normal People” is contemporary - romantic-tragic - comic - fresh - psychologically sharp - emotional - and very perceptive. <br />Rooney leaves me lingering in her characters. They are flawed and frustrated. <br />I ‘felt’ flawed and frustrated reading it! At times I wanted to scream at the characters - other times my heart just broke. <br /><br />I knew I wanted to read this novel. I even knew it would most likely drive me into my head. ( it did). <br />I’m not sure why I didn’t open it last year. <br />The book-cover alone has that ‘curl-up-and-get- sucked-in- feeling’, to it. <br />And that’s exactly what happened. <br />I COULD NOT STOP READING. ‘Addicted’! <br />I will never doubt my own gut desire again when it comes to a Sally Rooney novel. <br />I’m a fan here to stay. <br />Totally love what she creates. <br /><br />SOMETHING HAS SHIFTED IN ME, too, with respect to romance novels. I can no longer say...<br />“Oh, I don’t read romance novels”... It depends...<br />Heck, “Crime and Punishment”, had romance. Loaded with power and cruelty... but still some romance. <br />“East of Eden”, by John Steinbeck was filled with juicy romance...( destructive force)... but still...lust and romance was present. <br />Helen Hoang’s book, “The Kiss Quotient”, more modern, had romance written all over it. I loved it, too. <br /><br />Laugh at me if you wish...<br />but in the same way that I got hooked on the two main characters, ( Tessa and Hardin), in Anna Todd’s “After Series”.....( also a young author like Sally Rooney)....<br />I was hooked on the relationship’ between Connell and Marianne in “Normal People”. <br />I’m sure that Rooney would not turn this book into a series… but if she did, I’d read it. <br /><br />The electricity and entanglement between this Connell and Marianne - was soooo complex. I wanted to join their conversations about their families—about the way each felt about themselves, and each other.... and all the things that were happening to them. <br />When I finished the last page, my mind continued swimming in thoughts. <br />Most, I was sad to leave them. <br /><br />Soooo many fabulous sentences - page after page. Gorgeous reflective and intimate writing. <br />Sally Rooney is an ‘it’ author for me. <br /><br />LOVED IT!!!! ....<br />Ha... if you can’t tell. <br /><br />I’ll end with one expert:<br /> “All these years they’ve been like two little plants sharing the same pot of soil, growing around one another, contorting to make room, taking certain unlikely positions”. <br /><br /><br /><br /><br /><br /><br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="561271467641569558" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<span id="freeTextContainer16952171251665609576">What?! The.... what?! 😬😬😬😬 This book has been very publicized with the new Hulu adaptation and all. I for one, was looking forward to reading this one. Along with everyone else (judging by how long I waited in the library queue😡). Sadly, it didn’t live up to the hype for me. ☹️These characters were not likable. They both have clear issues, but I’ve read plenty of books where the characters are flawed but you still root for them in the end. And don’t even get me started on the ending. 🙄<br/></span>

<div id="review_2640048197" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2640048197" />
    <a title="Nilufer Ozmekik" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/53701594-nilufer-ozmekik"><img alt="Nilufer Ozmekik" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1559807601p2/53701594.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2640048197?book_show_action=true">Jan 23, 2019</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Nilufer Ozmekik" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Nilufer Ozmekik" href="/user/show/53701594-nilufer-ozmekik">Nilufer Ozmekik</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2640048197" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer9515977553383491762">Wow! Check out Hulu’s marvelous adaptation! They did amazing job by adapting this lyrical, poignant, sad and realistic story with remarkable, heartfelt performances! It is a real soul crusher, heartbreaker! Get ready to set your ugly cries free!!!!<br/><br/>This really reminded me of those tear jerkers, Oh God I cannot breathe, all my happiness swept away by emotional vampires vacuum cleaners inc., come on, that’s kind of nerve bending story that one of the protagonist has to die from a deadly disease ( o</span>
  <span id="freeText9515977553383491762" style="display:none">Wow! Check out Hulu’s marvelous adaptation! They did amazing job by adapting this lyrical, poignant, sad and realistic story with remarkable, heartfelt performances! It is a real soul crusher, heartbreaker! Get ready to set your ugly cries free!!!!<br /><br />This really reminded me of those tear jerkers, Oh God I cannot breathe, all my happiness swept away by emotional vampires vacuum cleaners inc., come on, that’s kind of nerve bending story that one of the protagonist has to die from a deadly disease ( or both of them needed to die sometimes! Oh no another crying torrent coming up! I cannot hold it! I can’t)or one of them has to commit suicide kind of, depressive, sad, exhausting, giving you anxiety attacks kind of John Green books. (After looking for Alaska, I felt the a dark cloud always following me for one month and my husband fed me with soap and Chardonnay, as you can imagine I couldn’t eat solid food at least two months because I bit the pages of the book and chewed so hard, destroyed my dental implements!!!)<br /><br />So yes this book is sad, horrifyingly bringing your dark clouds and vultures above your head and interesting fact is nobody dies! But yes there are so many heavy, harsh, heart wrenching, brain cell boiling issues make you feel like hit by a truck several times, then suffered from waterboarding and torture conducted by American Psycho’s Patrick Bateman and finally thrown away into the swamp,eaten by crocodiles. The characters deal with drug addiction, bullying, sexual assault, suicidal thoughts, severe depression and it is really heartbreaking to see them not to have a regular teenager lives.<br /><br /> And you know what after all those torturous feelings, my kindest part of soul( also my masochist brain cells and my vulnerable heart) loved those two characters, Connell and Marianne and witnessed their literally growing up, their adolescence and early adulthood times, forming friendship, special- sensitive bound. At first when they were in high school, Marianne is outcast, social pariah, bullied by mean girls as Connell is shiny, popular star of the school community. The part he didn’t take her to the prom was harsh, mean move and Connell lost his all his brownie points and earned slapping contest championship’s high rated asshole statue.<br /><br /> But when they were in college, the balances were changed now Marianne is intellectual, independent, smart social queen and Connell loses his spotlight and sentenced to be an ordinary, invisible college boy which makes him more depressed and lonely.<br /><br />Their friends-lovers- again friends- again lovers kind of complex relationship and their story’s revelation should be called : “Restrained screams” or “Unsaid Words” , or “Bottled Up Emotions!” or “I think I’m really pissed off those two characters so much for breaking my heart !”<br />I know the realistic conclusion was necessary, logical, reasonable but it doesn’t mean it is not hurting you so much!<br /><br />As a result, if you can deal with feeling blue by reading sad, sad, sad, OH GOD WHY THE HELL I CARED SO MUCH ABOUT THOSE CHARACTERS kind of book, this is just for you.<br /><br />I liked the captivating, realistic, poignant story telling and I truly accepted those broken, flawed, complex characters but I think sometimes their story made me suffocated a little. This is a good book but not my first choice of reading<br /><br /><a href="https://niluferozmekik.com/" rel="nofollow noopener">blog</a><br /><a href="https://www.instagram.com/nilylovestoread/" rel="nofollow noopener">instagram</a><br /><a href="https://www.facebook.com/nilufer.ozmekik" rel="nofollow noopener">facebook</a><br /><a href="https://twitter.com/NiluferOzmekik" rel="nofollow noopener">twitter</a></span>
  <a data-text-id="9515977553383491762" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

<div id="review_3305163176" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/3305163176" />
    <a title="Ali Abdaal" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/45329045-ali-abdaal"><img alt="Ali Abdaal" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1490308900p2/45329045.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/3305163176?book_show_action=true">Apr 27, 2020</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Ali Abdaal" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Ali Abdaal" href="/user/show/45329045-ali-abdaal">Ali Abdaal</a>
      </span>

        rated it

<div id="review_2806099596" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2806099596" />
    <a title="emma" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/32879029-emma"><img alt="emma" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1520568130p2/32879029.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2806099596?book_show_action=true">May 30, 2019</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="emma" class="user" itemprop="url" name="emma" href="/user/show/32879029-emma">emma</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Hardcover 9780571334643" href="/book/show/37539457-normal-people">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/32879029-emma?shelf=couldn-t-wait-to-read">couldn-t-wait-to-read</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/32879029-emma?shelf=auto-buy-authors">auto-buy-authors</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/32879029-emma?shelf=literary-fiction">literary-fiction</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/32879029-emma?shelf=beautifully-written">beautifully-written</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/32879029-emma?shelf=reviewed">reviewed</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/32879029-emma?shelf=recommend">recommend</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/32879029-emma?shelf=owned">owned</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/32879029-emma?shelf=non-ya">non-ya</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/32879029-emma?shelf=i-love-these-characters">i-love-these-characters</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/32879029-emma?shelf=4-stars">4-stars</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2806099596" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer8777542851825731905"><i>“Life offers up these moments of joy despite everything.”</i><br/><br/>The first time I read this, I rated it three stars. While this can be considered relatively high for me (don’t check my average rating, it will only bring despair to us both), it is approximately two stars lower than what I expected to rate this book.<br/><br/>I adore Rooney’s prior novel, Conversations with Friends, to a degree that is almost disturbing. Or possibly just disturbing.<br/><br/>But this one fell flat for me. In a way that was difficult, at the </span>
  <span id="freeText8777542851825731905" style="display:none"><i>“Life offers up these moments of joy despite everything.”</i><br /><br />The first time I read this, I rated it three stars. While this can be considered relatively high for me (don’t check my average rating, it will only bring despair to us both), it is approximately two stars lower than what I expected to rate this book.<br /><br />I adore Rooney’s prior novel, Conversations with Friends, to a degree that is almost disturbing. Or possibly just disturbing.<br /><br />But this one fell flat for me. In a way that was difficult, at the time, to put a finger on. While I encountered the same stellar, almost painful writing, and the same reading experience so all-encompassing that it felt like it changed something fundamental about me, while I loved the characters so much that my concern for their well-being stressed me out, I did not come away from this book in love.<br /><br />I put a finger on what the thing keeping me and this book away from eternal love and matrimony was. <br /><br />It’s because I was sad.<br /><br />The first time I read this, I was so wrapped up in the characters and their lives and my concern for them that I overlooked...everything else. To me this was the story of Connell and Marianne and nothing else, and while I adored them both I missed out on the multitude of nuances and themes and symbols at play. The treatment of privilege and wealth, the examination of capitalism through relationships, the look at what love and self-worth mean, the submission and sometimes humiliation that is love.<br /><br />This is a gorgeous book, and a beautifully written one, and the second read of this enthralled me so much I lived in the story for a week.<br /><br />For once, I’m at a loss for what else to say.<br /><br />Bottom line: I was wrong, okay!!! There’s a first time for everything.<br /><br />p.s. In the original review I say that I'll never reread this book. That wrongness counts as the same one.<br /><br />---------<br /><i>reread pre-review</i><br /><br />raising this from 3 to 4 stars upon reread, so guess i have to rewrite this review.<br /><br />oh, the twists and turns life takes.<br /><br />review to come / 4 stars<br /><br />---------<br /><i>reread currently-reading updates</i><br /><br />maybe someday i will be the kind of person who doesn't take every excuse to reread, but today is not that day<br /><br />---------<br /><i>original review</i><br /><br />When I finished this book, I didn’t even rate it. I couldn’t. I had no clue how to even approach such a thing.<br /><br />I still don’t.<br /><br />That’s because I loved reading every single word of this (because every single word of this was written by Sally Rooney), but I also, in a much more real way, did not enjoy at all.<br /><br /><a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2831723058?book_show_action=false&amp;from_review_page=1" rel="nofollow noopener">Conversations with Friends</a>, which I five starred, reread just a few months after my first read, and have not stopped thinking about, is not an easy book to read. I adore it, but I did not enjoy every second of it.<br /><br />Far from it, actually. That book’s characters are part of my heart, but I didn’t necessarily <i>like</i> them. I felt intensely and deeply known by its story, and that process doesn’t necessarily feel like a walk in a park. <br /><br />Well, maybe it is. But on one of those days where when you first go outside the temperature is perfect in a long-sleeve shirt, but then you spend every minute outside growing slightly chillier to the point of discomfort. And you’re excited to see the park has little ice-cream carts, but then you realize the process of eating the ice cream ultimately won’t live up to your imagining of it, and you don’t really like ice cream all that much anyway.<br /><br />If that’s Conversations with Friends…<br /><br />Normal People is a walk in a park during a blizzard. Without a jacket. And to distract yourself you have an ongoing internal monologue that’s actually sort of brilliant, you’re in rare form, and that’s great and all but it’s not quite enough to distract from the fact that all of this seems pointless and rather painful.<br /><br />It really seems to me that Rooney abandoned the gorgeous, deep characterizations and slow-moving stories of Conversations in favor of making characters vessels for themes.<br /><br />And I’ve simply never been that kind of a reader. I read FOR the characters, not around them.<br /><br />I didn’t much care for Connell and Marianne, nor their romance (if you can call it that). I couldn’t click with their arcs or their escapades or much of anything, besides Rooney’s writing. (Which was unchangedly amazing and possibly even better.)<br /><br />There were also some things about this that made me feel...icky. Sexual submission (specifically Marianne’s) is used as a metaphor here, and never kindly. This behavior of hers is presented as negative, usually, but it’s also inarguable that Marianne is submissive in her relationship with Connell, and that is never resolved. Connell feels unhappy several times over about the degree of her power over her, and while they return to their relationship contentedly towards the end, this is not at all resolved.<br /><br />I missed the lovely, tied-strings ending of Conversations.<br /><br />Conversations made me feel heard, made my heart and brain feel full, and Normal People made me feel...almost dumb. As if I was missing something that would have helped me put it all together, and without it of course it felt incomplete, silly, because I didn’t have the intellectual capacity to complete it.<br /><br />It’s possible this just isn’t the book I needed, when Conversations with Friends certainly was.<br /><br />It was still written by Sally Rooney, though.<br /><br />Bottom line: I will never reread this. Also I desperately need more Rooney.<br /><br />---------<br /><i>pre-review</i><br /><br />i......cannot even rate this right now.<br /><br />review to come, when i regain the ability to think<br /><br />---------<br /><br />i want Sally Rooney to write my internal monologue</span>
  <a data-text-id="8777542851825731905" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_2677069328" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2677069328" />
    <a title="Meredith" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/30978160-meredith"><img alt="Meredith" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1423329725p2/30978160.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2677069328?book_show_action=true">Aug 24, 2019</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Meredith" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Meredith" href="/user/show/30978160-meredith">Meredith</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/30978160-meredith?shelf=overdrive">overdrive</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2677069328" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer9955613700103848066"><b>
  <i>Uncomfortable and Provocative<br/><br/>In Normal People, Sally Rooney tells the story of two deeply damaged people who develop an intense relationship that transcends the norms. </i>
</b><br/><br/>Connell and Marianne start a secret romantic relationship while in high school. Connell is the popular jock who secretly cares what everyone thinks about him. Marianne is the school pariah--the girl who people create myths about. While they both feel alone and misunderstood, together they understand not only one another, but a</span>
  <span id="freeText9955613700103848066" style="display:none"><b>
  <i>Uncomfortable and Provocative<br /><br />In Normal People, Sally Rooney tells the story of two deeply damaged people who develop an intense relationship that transcends the norms. </i>
</b><br /><br />Connell and Marianne start a secret romantic relationship while in high school. Connell is the popular jock who secretly cares what everyone thinks about him. Marianne is the school pariah--the girl who people create myths about. While they both feel alone and misunderstood, together they understand not only one another, but also themselves. When they start University, their roles reverse. No longer forced to keep their relationship a secret, they have other barriers to face--many which are dark and daunting. Both begin to spiral. It is only when they are together that they can face themselves and the world around them.<br /><br /><i>Normal People</i> could have been a whiny, angsty read about two very self-absorbed 18-to twenty-somethings, but the narrative structure and Rooney's writing elevates the characters and story to another level. <br /><br />The narrative is told through the inner workings of Connell and Marianne’s minds. The reader is privy to their issues and disturbing thoughts. <b>They are awkward and flawed characters, which made them feel very real.</b> I was hoping for more growth, but the glimpse of hope at the end helped me realize that Connell and Marianne were ready to face the future. <b>This is a very dark and disturbing read with some light at the end. While I came to care about Connell and Marianne’s characters, I wouldn’t want to read this again! </b><br /><br /><b>
  <i>“I don’t know why I can’t be like normal people.”</i>
</b><br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="9955613700103848066" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>
